TB Resolution 2025-234 
 
ASSUMES LEAD AGENCY, ISSUES CONDITIONAL NEGATIVE DECLARATION 
FOR THE SITE PLAN APPLICATION OF ISLAND WATER PARK (D/B/A SCOTT'S 
POINTE) 5835 MIDDLE COUNTRY ROAD, CALVERTON, NY SCTM NO. 600-135-1-
7.34 
 
Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
WHEREAS, the Riverhead Town Board is in receipt of a site plan application 
seeking to amend the previously approved site plan of Island Water Park (d/b/a Scott’s 
Pointe); and  
 
 WHEREAS, the proposed amendments include legalization of a go -kart track, 
pickleball courts, and conversion of an existing interior storage space of use as a 
catering/event space; and  
 
 WHEREAS, by Resolution No. 2024 -996, dated De cember 17, 2024, the Town 
Board classified the site plan application as an Unlisted action pursuant to SEQRA, and 
initiated coordinated review among involved agencies in accordance with 6NYCRR Part 
617.6(b)(3); and  
 
 WHEREAS, the Planning Department, on D ecember 18, 2024, distributed 
SEQRA coordination materials to the following involved agencies: 
 
1. Suffolk County Planning Commission 
2. Suffolk County Department of Health Services 
3. New York State Department of Environmental Conservation 
4. Riverhead Water District  
5. Riverhead Fire Marshal’s Office 
6. Riverhead Industrial Development Agency; and  
 
WHEREAS, in a letter dated November 25, 2024, H2M Architects + Engineers, 
consulting engineer for the Riverhead Water District, indicated that Key Money would be 
assessed for the change in use of the building, with total Key Money fees being 
$84,220.50, where $68,723.20 had already been paid to the District, leaving a balance 
of $15,497.30 due to the District upon approval of the amended site plan application; 
and 
 
 WHEREAS, in a letter dated January 31, 2025, the Suffolk County Planning 
Commission considered the application to be a matter for local determination, and 
offered the following comments: 
 
1. Pursuant to NYS General Municipal Law §239 and Suffolk County 
Administrative Code §A14-14 actions subject to referral includes the adoption 
9.25
Packet Pg. 180
or amendment of a comprehensive plan, zoning ordinance or local law, the 
issuance of a special use permit, approval of a site plan, the granting of area 
or use variances or other authorizations p rior to making a final determination.  
Site plan such as the ones dated 11/18/21 should have been referred to the 
Suffolk County Planning Commission before being approved by the Town. 
 
2. Though the outdoor go -kart track and pickleball courts appear to have b een 
constructed between March and June of 2024; the applicant should be 
encouraged to incorporate green methodologies such as rain gardens, 
bioswales, etc. as described in the Suffolk County Planning Commission 
publication on Managing Stormwater -Natural Ve getation and Green 
Methodologies, as an additional tool to manage stormwater runoff. 
 
3. Whenever possible commercial buildings should incorporate the use of 
renewable energy through utilization of rooftop solar, wind and/or geothermal 
systems; or at minimum be built solar ready. 
 
4. Information pertaining to a proposed lighting plan for the go -cart track and 
pickleball courts was not included with referral materials.  Should the 
petitioner with to include lighting to illuminate the existing go -cart track and 
pickleball courts, all exterior lighting should conform to standards and 
requirements specified in the Town Code.  
 
5. All new development with parking lots should include plans for (2%) of off -
street parking stalls to become future electric vehicle charging stations.  
 
6. All new development with parking lots should designate a minimum (8%) of 
parking spaces for clean energy vehicles but should not increase the number 
of parking spaces beyond the minimum required to provide such 
designations. 
 
7. Please be advised that our agency, the Suffolk County Planning Commission, 
has no objection to the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead assuming Lead 
Agency status for the above referenced [action/site plan]; and  
 
WHEREAS, in a letter dated January 29, 2025, the New York State  Department 
of Environmental Conservation stated the following: 
 
Be advised, this agency does not accept or process applications for existing 
structures and we do not issue after -the-fact permits for existing structures 
located within regulated areas.  Str uctures built within a regulated area without 
benefit of a DEC permit is either a violation of the Environmental Conservation 
Law (ECL) or it did not require a permit.  Permits must be obtained prior to any 
work activities taking place.  
 
On April 11, 2023, DEC received a Mining Permit Application requesting renewal 
of an Article 23 permit as the property owner required additional time for 
reclamation efforts.  DEC may have additional comments at a later date as this 
application is currently undergoing technical review. 
 
DEC has the following comments: 
 
9.25
Packet Pg. 181
1. If this event space is new or otherwise not included on the SPDES application 
being reviewed by Suffolk County Department of Health Services, the permit 
would need modification before Island Water Park is auth orized to discharge 
wastewater from this portion of the project. 
 
2. Portion of New York State regulated freshwater wetlands and their adjacent 
areas may be located in the project area.  Although some limited activities are 
exempt from permitting, most activi ties that involve disturbance within a 
wetland or its 100 -foot adjacent area require an Environmental Conservation 
Law (ECL) Article 24, Freshwater Wetlands permit from the DEC.  Information 
on regulated activities within freshwater wetlands and adjacent a reas is 
available on DEC’s website (see Regulated Activities), which contains 
examples of regulated activities and those exempt from wetland permits.  
 
DEC’s amended Article 24, Freshwater Wetlands Jurisdiction and Classification 
regulations (6 NYCRR Part 664) went into effect on January 1, 2025.  To 
determine whether the property contains regulated freshwater wetlands, the 
project sponsor must submit a request for a Parcel Jurisdictional Determination 
(Parcel JD).  A Parcel JD is a determination made by DE C whether a property 
contains regulated freshwater wetlands or adjacent areas within the parcel 
boundary.  Please use the attached link to request a Parcel JD for the project 
site: https://dec.ny.gov/nature/waterbodies/wetlands/freshwater-wetlands-
program/freshwater-wetland-jurisdictional-determination.  If you have any 
problems submitting the Parcel JD request, please e mail: 
fwwjurisdiction@dec.ny.gov. 
 
If the property contains regulated freshwater wetlands or adjacent areas, further 
delineation of the wetland boundaries and a Project Jurisdictional Determination 
(Project JD) may be required.  A Project JD is a determination made by DEC 
whether a proposed activity within a parcel containing regulated freshwater 
wetlands or adjacent areas requires an Article 24 Freshwater Wetlands permit.  If 
necessary, a Project JD may als o be requested using the link provided above.  If 
regulated freshwater wetlands or adjacent areas are present, all efforts must be 
made to first avoid disturbing the wetland and adjacent area.  If disturbance to 
the wetland and/or adjacent area cannot be a voided, the project sponsor must 
submit a Freshwater Wetland permit application, and obtain a permit to conduct a 
regulated activity.  In accordance with DEC’s Freshwater Wetlands Permit 
Requirements Regulations (6 NYCRR Part 663), the applicant would need  to 
justify the disturbance, discuss alternatives and minimize impacts as part of the 
Freshwater Wetlands permit application.  More information on application 
procedures and permit issuance standards is available on ’EC's website at: 
https://dec.ny.gov/regulatory/permits-licenses/waterways-coastlines-
wetlands/freshwater-wetlands#Determnine. 
 
3. DEC has concerns regarding the possibility o f spillage from the track to enter 
surface waters.  Since this would be an unintended and intermittent 
discharge, it is not something that DEC would regulate under a SPDES 
Permit.  Instead, this would likely be handled on a case -by-case basis with 
possible violations if/when these discharges were to occur.  To avoid potential 
violations, DEC suggests the applicant implement Best Management 
Practices around the track/edge of water to further reduce the risk for 
anything running off of the track an into the water; and  
9.25
Packet Pg. 182
 
WHEREAS, in a letter dated January 3, 2025, the Suffolk County Department of 
Health Services had the following comments: 
 
1. Sanitary Code: 
 
A: Article VI Application Status : The Department has not received a 
commercial wastewater application for the above referenced project, as 
required by Article VI of the Suffolk County Sanitary Code.  The project 
sponsor should submit an application to our agency’s Office of 
Wastewater Management at the earliest possible date so that a complete 
technical assessment of this proposal can be undertaken. 
 
B.  SCDHS Jurisdiction :  The SCDHS maintains jurisdiction over the final 
use and size of the property.  The applicant, therefore, should not 
undertake the subdivision without Health Department approval.  Density 
and complete site plan details are essential to the review of this project.  
These considerations are reviewed completely at the time of SCDHS 
application; and

following comments: 
 
1. Emergency Responder radio coverage system must be completed in existing 
building. 
 
2. An additional fire hydrant will be required if there is an exterior storage for 
flammable gas further than 400 feet from existing hydrant. 507.1 Required 
Water Supply – An approved water supply capable of supplying the required 
fire flow for fire protection shall be provided to premises on which facilities, 
building or portions of buildings are hereafter constructed or moved into or 
within the jurisdiction.  FACILITY. A bu ilding or use in a fixed location 
including exterior storage areas for flammable and combustible substances 
and hazardous materials, piers, wharves, tank farms and similar uses.  This 
term includes recreational vehicles, mobile home and manufactured housin g 
parks, sales and storage lots.

operations at motorsports venues; and

application, shall eliminate or mitigate any potentially signific ant adverse impacts on the 
environment: 
 
1. The applicant shall submit an as -built, topographic survey of the pickleball 
courts and go-kart track, and shall submit an amended grading and drainage 
plan demonstrating retention and capture of all stormwater, wit h same being 
prevented from entering the pond. 
 
2. The use of the track shall be limited to go -karts, as stated by the applicant in 
their submittals, and that the use of the track for any other type of vehicle 
shall be prohibited.  This restriction shall be r ecorded as a covenant against 
the subject property by the applicant. 
 
3. The applicant shall amend the site plan to identify fuel storage area, shall 
implement spill protection measures, shall maintain on -site a spill response 
kit, and shall proposed a spill response plan in order to capture and contain 
spills of any materials that may occur on site.  
 
4. Groundwater monitoring, as agreed to by the applicant, and as recorded with 
the Suffolk County Clerk on October 31, 2024 under Liber D00013270, Page 
495, shall continue on the property for the duration of the agreement period.  
 
5. The applicant shall submit to the NYSDEC a Parcel Jurisdictional 
Determination and shall submit the results of the NYSDEC Jurisdictional 
Determination to the Town. 
 
6. The applicant must rec eive approval from the Suffolk County Department of 
Health Services Office of Wastewater Management; and be it further

9.26.a
Packet Pg. 201
Attachment: Notice of Adoption Chapter 207 Animal license fees [Revision 1]  (2025-235 : Adopts a Local Law Amending Chapter 207 of the
Chapter 207. Animals 
 
Article I. Dogs and Domestic/Farm Animals 
 
§ 207-3. Application for license. 
 
A.  Applications for a one -year license or a renewal thereof shall be accompanied by a 
nonrefundable processing fee of $9 for an altered dog and $15  for an unaltered dog. 
Applications for a three -year license or renewal thereof shall be accompanied by a 
nonrefundable processing fee of $27 for an altered dog and $45 for an unaltered dog  
established by resolution of the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead. In the case of an 
altered dog, a portion of the fee in the amount of $1 and, in the case of an unaltered dog, 
a portion of the fee in the amount of $3 shall be paid over to the agency designated 
pursuant to Article 7 of the Agriculture and Markets Law to be used for animal population 
control efforts. An application for a license or renewal shall be in the form prescribed by 
the Riverhead Town Clerk and shall provide for the following minimum information: 
 
(1) The name, residence address and telephone number of each owner; 
 
(2) The name, sex, approximate age, breed, color, markings and other identifying details 
of the dog; 
 
(3) Whether the dog has been spayed or neutered; and 
 
(4) Such other information or documentation deemed necessary by the Town Clerk to 
effectuate the purpose of this article. 
 
B. Rabies certification. The application for a license or renewal shall be accompanied by 
a statement certified by a licensed veterinarian showing that the dog has received the 
rabies vaccine; or, in lieu thereof, a statement certified by a licensed veterinarian that 
because of the dog's age or other reason, the life of the dog would be endangered by the 
administration of the vaccine. 
 
C. In the case of an altered dog, every application shall be accompanied by a certificate 
signed by a licensed veterinarian or a sworn affidavit signed by the owner in the form 
acceptable to the Town Clerk showing that the dog has been spayed or neutered, except 
that such certificate or affidavit is not required if same is already on file with the Town 
Clerk. In lieu of the spay or neuter certificate, an owner may present a statement certified 
by a licensed veterinarian stating that he or she has examined the dog and found that 
because of old age or other reason, the life of the dog would be endangered by spaying 
or neutering. In such case, the license fee for the dog shall be the same as an altered 
dog. 
 
D. No individual under the age of 18 years shall be deemed an owner of record and be 
issued a dog license. 
 
§ 207-4. Issuance of license; transferability; identification tag. 
 
A. Upon validation by the Town Clerk or authorized Dog Control Officer, a dog license 
shall be issued and a record of its issuance retained in the office of the Town Clerk. Such 
9.26.b
Packet Pg. 202
Attachment: Chapter 207 Full Text Animal fees  (2025-235 : Adopts a Local Law Amending Chapter 207 of the Riverhead Town Code Titled,
record shall be made available upon request to the State Commissioner of Agric ulture 
and Markets, or successor thereof. 
 
B. No license shall be transferable. Upon the transfer of ownership of any dog, the new 
owner shall immediately apply for a new license for the dog. A license cannot be 
transferred to another dog. 
 
C. Identification tag. 
 
(1) The Town Clerk shall assign an identification number to a dog when it is first 
licensed. Such identification number shall be carried by the dog on an identification 
tag which shall be affixed to the collar of the dog at all times, except that the tag is 
not required to be worn while the dog is participating in a dog show. In addition, all 
identification tags shall name the Town of Riverhead, 200 Howell Avenue, 
Riverhead, New York State 11901, and name the Town of Riverhead's main 
telephone number. 
 
(2)  No tag carrying an identification number shall be affixed to the collar of any dog 
other than the one to which the number has been assigned. 
 
(3)  Any person wishing to replace a tag previously issued shall pay the sum of $3 
established by resolution of the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead to the Town 
Clerk for a replacement tag. 
 
§ 207-11. Redemption of impounded dogs. 
 
A. Unidentified dogs. Each dog which is not identified, whether or not licensed, shall be 
held for a period of five days from the day seized. 
 
(1) During the first five days the dog may be redeemed by its owner, provided that 
such owner produces proof that the dog has been licensed and has been identified 
pursuant to the provisions of Article 7 of the New York State Agriculture and 
Markets Law, as well as the following impoundment fees established by resolution 
of the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead. 
 
(a) Twenty Twenty-five dollars for the first impoundment of any dog owned by that 
person. 
 
(b) Forty dollars for the first 24 hours or part thereof and $5 for each additional 24 
hours or part thereof for the second impoundment within one year of the first 
impoundment of any dog owned by that person. 
(c) Sixty dollars for the first 24 hours or part thereof and $5 for each additional 24 
hours or part thereof for the third and subsequent impoundments within one year 
of the first impoundment of any dog owned by that person. 
 
* Underline represents addition(s) 
* Overstrike represents deletion(s)

Chapter 257. Peddling and Soliciting 
Article I. Licensing and Regulation 
§ 257-7. Fees. 
 
A.  
The license fee payable by each peddler for each unit, truck or any conveyance carrying 
wares shall be established by resolution of the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead. as 
follows: 
(1)  
Per year: $100. 
(2)  
Per six months: $75. 
(3)  
Per three months: $50. 
B.  
The license fee for each solicitor or canvasser going from house to house shall be 
established by resolution of the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead. as follows: 
(1)  
Per year: $75. 
(2)  
Per six months: $50. 
(3)  
Per three months: $25.

Packet Pg. 209
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
NOTICE OF ADOPTION  
 
PLEASE TAKE NOTICE, that the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead adopted 
a local law to amend Chapter 301 of the Riverhead Town Code titled “ZONING AND LAND 
DEVELOPMENT §301 -229. YARD SALES, ATTIC SALES, GARAGE SALES AND 
AUCTION SALES” at its regular meeting held on February 19, 2025. 
  
The intent of the proposed amendment is to remove the fees from the code and provide 
that such fees shall be set by Town Board Resolution.  
 A copy of the entire text of the adopted local law may be reviewed at the Office of 
the Town Clerk, 4 West Second Street, Riverhead, New York 11901, between the hours 
of 8:30 a.m. and 4:30 p.m., Monday through Friday and can be accessed on the Town of 
Riverhead website at: www.townofriverheadny.gov under the Agenda and Minutes for the 
March 4, 2025 Town Board Meeting.  
 
Dated:  Riverhead, New York 
         March 4, 2025  
 
BY ORDER OF THE TOWN BOARD 
OF THE TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
JAMES WOOTEN, Town Clerk 
 
 
9.28.a
Packet Pg. 210
Attachment: Notice to Adopt Chapter 301 Yard Sale fees [Revision 1]  (2025-237 : Adopts a Local Law Amending Chapter 301 Yard Sale Fees)
Chapter 301. Zoning and Land Development 
Part 3. Supplementary Regulations 
Article XLV. Supplementary Use Regulations 
 
§ 301-229. Yard sales, attic sales, garage sales and auction sales. 
 
B.  
Registration; fee. 
 
(1) Prior to any operator holding such sales within any calendar year, such operator 
must register the dates and location with the Town of Riverhead. 
 
(2) A registration form shall be obtained therefor from the Town Clerk. 
 
(3) A fee established by resolution of the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead of $5 
shall be required for each permit issued. 
 
* Underline represents addition(s) 
* Overstrike represents deletion(s)

TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-238 
 
RATIFIES AUTHORIZATION FOR THE SUPERVISOR TO EXECUTE AN 
AGREEMENT WITH THE RIVERHEAD TOWN POLICE BENEVOLENT 
ASSOCIATION 
 
Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Town Board approves the 
agreement between the Riverhead Town Police Benevolent Association ("PBA") and the 
Town of Riverhead for the contract period January 1, 2023 through December 31, 2026 and 
ratifies the authorization for the Town Supervisor to execute same, and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby authorized to forward a copy of this 
resolution to the Financial Administrator, the Personnel Director, the PBA President, the 
Chief of Police and the Office of the Town Attorney; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of this 
resolution from the electronic storage device and if needed, a certified copy of same may be 
obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.

03.04.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-239 
 
AUTHORIZES SUBMISSION OF APPLICATION FOR BODY ARMOR VESTS FOR 
CODE ENFORCEMENT OFFICERS 
 
Councilman Kern offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Merrifield 
 
WHEREAS, the Code Enforcement Officer Safety Foundation, a Non -Profit 
Charity provides body armor vests for use by Code Enforcement Officers through its 
Request a Vest program; and  
  
 WHEREAS, the Town of Riverhead is eligible to receive 10 vests to be used by  
inspectors in the Code Enforcement Department and the Fire Marshal’s Office upon 
approval of an application submitted to the Code Enforcement Safety Foundation; and 
 
 WHEREAS, the Town Board wishes to receive the body armor vests with an 
approximate value  of $20,000.000 for the safety and protection of the Town’s Code 
Enforcement Officers and Fire Marshals. 
 
 NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Riverhead Town Board hereby 
authorizes the Community Development Division to prepare and submit an applicati on 
to the Code Enforcement Officer Safety Foundation for 10 body armor vests to be used 
by Town of Riverhead Code Enforcement Officers and Fire Marshals; and be it further, 
 
 RESOLVED that a copy of this resolution shall be forwarded to the Community 
Development Division, Office of the Town Attorney, Accounting Department, Code 
Enforcement and the Fire Marshal’s Office; and be it further, 
 
 RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a certified copy of 
same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Robert Kern, Councilman 
SECONDER: Denise Merrifield, Councilwoman 
AYES: Kenneth Rothwell, Robert Kern, Denise Merrifield, Joann Waski 
ABSENT: Tim Hubbard

03.04.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-240 
 
RATIFY THE RESCINDING OF TOWN BOARD RESOLUTION 2022-181 AND TOWN 
BOARD RESOLUTION 2022-723 
 
Councilwoman Merrifield offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Waski 
 
WHEREAS, pursuant to Town Board Resolution 2022 -181, the Town Board 
selected Joint Venture entity between RXR and Georgica Green Ventures (“GGV”), 
collectively as the Master Developer for the Transit Oriented Development Projects One 
and Two; and 
 
WHEREAS, pursuant to Town Board Resolution 2022 -674, a Qualified and 
Eligible sponsorship public hearing was scheduled for September 27, 2022; and 
 
WHEREAS, pursuant to Town Board Resolution 2022 -723, a Qualified and 
Eligible sponsorship public hearing was held o n September 27, 2022 and Joint Venture 
entity between RXR and Georgica Green Ventures (“GGV”) was deemed qualified and 
eligible and authorized the Supervisor and the Director of the Community Development 
Agency to execute the Master Development Agreement; and 
 
WHEREAS, by letter from RXR and GGV dated February 26, 2025, the Town 
was notified, that “while the Master Developer Agreement was approved by the Town of 
Riverhead, it was never fully executed and delivered and therefore is not a binding 
agreement on any party.”; and 
 
WHEREAS, in light of this position, the Town wishes to rescind the above -
mentioned Town Board Resolutions. 
   
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED,  that the Riverhead Town Board hereby 
rescinds Town Board Resolution 2022 -181 and Town Board Resol ution 2022 -723 
effective February 26, 2025; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby directed to forward a copy of this 
resolution to the Office of the Town Attorney and the Community Development Agency; 
Joint Venture Entity Between RXR a nd GGV c/o RXR, 625 RXR Plaza, Uniondale, NY 
11556 Attention: Joe Graziose, Graziose@rxr.com; Georgica Green Ventures, LLC, 50 
Jericho Quadrangle, Suite 118, Jericho, NY 11753 Attention: David Gallo, 
davidgallo@georgicagreen.com; and be it further 
 
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and 
obtain a copy of this resolution from the electronic storage device, and if needed, a 
certified copy of same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
THE VOTE
